  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

One night was all it took, and I forgot everything and anything except the sexy fighter in the ring who sets my mind ablaze and my body on fire with wanting...<br /><br />Remington Tate is the strongest, most confusing man I've ever met in my life.<br /><br />He’s the star of the dangerous underground fighting circuit, and I’m drawn to him as I've never been drawn to anything in my life. I forget who I am, what I want, with just one look from him. When he’s near, I need to remind myself that I am strong—but he is stronger. And now it’s my job to keep his body working like a perfect machine, his taut muscles primed and ready to break the bones of his next opponents...<br /><br />But the one he’s most threatening to, now, is me.<br /><br />I want him. I want him without fear. Without reservations.<br /><br />If only I knew for sure what it is that he wants from me?</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/639518433" />
    <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden"><img alt="Katrina Passick Lumsden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416959676p2/1964146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/639518433?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katrina Passick Lumsden" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden">Katrina Passick Lumsden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden?shelf=run-away-quickly">run-away-quickly</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer639518433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13891765054399301985">Oh, how I wish this book were an underground boxing match. I've had so much fun thinking up names and special fighting techniques for Brooke and Remington. <br/><br/>Brooke "The Washout" Dumas. Weighing in at an arguably lithe 120lbs., Brooke's fighting style relies more on flexibility and trickery than sheer brute force. Having been denied her dream of Olympic gold thanks to an injury, Brooke's had years to save up all her bitter rage and coil it into a tight ball of hate that she's stuffed in "her core"</span>
  <span id="freeText13891765054399301985" style="display:none">Oh, how I wish this book were an underground boxing match. I've had so much fun thinking up names and special fighting techniques for Brooke and Remington. <br><br>Brooke "The Washout" Dumas. Weighing in at an arguably lithe 120lbs., Brooke's fighting style relies more on flexibility and trickery than sheer brute force. Having been denied her dream of Olympic gold thanks to an injury, Brooke's had years to save up all her bitter rage and coil it into a tight ball of hate that she's stuffed in "her core". Now she's wound tight and ready for action. Her hobbies are babbling incessantly about inane bullshit, stretching, and making stupid decisions. Turn ons are tacky tattoos, muscles, sweat, and mood swings. Her special skills include an almost unrealistic ability to contort her body (she can turn her head around and kiss a guy on the mouth while in the doggystyle position), and an overabundance of vaginal fluid which she directs at unsuspecting opponents. <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2wbubz4" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380425101ra/847992.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Seriously, get that woman some Depends before she kills someone.<br><br>Remington "RageTurd" Tate is just your typical, musclebound gorilla. <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=j0z5sm" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Ragey's actual size is never stated, but if my impressions are accurate, he's roughly the size of a small barn. Left to fend for himself in the "loony bin" at the tender age of 13, Ragey has learned how to fight, fight, fight his way to the top (of the orgy pile!). His most valuable talent in the ring is his ability to throw out Super Pheromone, which makes every straight female and gay male in a five mile radius stupid with lust. Senses are dulled and inhibitions are destroyed. His hobbies include fighting, yelling, raging, table flipping, lamp smashing, marking his territory with his urine, and sniffing every woman of mating age in his general vicinity. His turn ons are pert butts, "honeyed whiskey eyes", and women with vaginal fluid imbalances. <br><br>The book itself has its own killer instincts. There are enough metaphors to sink a yacht, and the staccato nearly reached <i>Fifty Shades</i> levels. Between that and the term "my sex", I was suffering some serious "bad erotica" flashbacks. Thankfully, there was enough unintentional funny to keep me from completely losing (the rest of) my mind. Some of it is funny because the bad grammar makes it weird. Other parts are funny merely because someone not only <i>thought</i> them, but thought they were good enough to put on paper. For instance, the first named opponent of Ragey is a guy by the name of Kirk Dirkwood. Why that was so funny to me, I couldn't tell ya, but I did make a note in my Kindle: "Why didn't she just go with Clit Dickwater?"<br><br>The various story arcs are usually pretty ridiculous. In one twist, Brooke sees her younger sister, Nora, "in the Underground". This occurs during a match between Remington and his arch-nemesis, The Scorpion. Last Brooke knew, Nora was sending their parents postcards from Australia, but alas, there she is on The Scorpion's side of the ring, looking strung-out, pale, skinny...and with a scorpion tattoo on her face.<br><br>You know where that's going, right? Well, Brooke <i>has</i> to rescue Nora from Snidely Whiplash, and since Remington, in a manic hissy fit, bet "all of his money" that he'd beat Scorpion in the "Underground Championship"....wouldn't it just be <i>so unbelievably sweet</i> if he threw the match to ensure Nora's release from El Scorpio?<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2i7ogly" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <b>"My legs wobble and I'm left with the distinct impression this man wants to pound me next. With his cock."<br><br>"He's so close the scent of him tears through me like a shot of adrenaline."<br><br>"I dip my head and murmur, "Thank you", and quickly leave, and I want to die because I swear to God he just ducked his head to smell me."<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2m6ltlt" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/583631.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>"I'm still not recovered from seeing him up close, and my blood stream already carries all kinds of strange, bubbly, hot little things."<br><br>"There is, literally, a ball of fire in my throat..."<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=1roruv" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1379793861ra/583632.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>"...and I'm so crazy about this man, I just want to eat him up with a spoon..."<br><br>"...and an entire farm full of animals awaken in my stomach, not just the butterflies."<br><br>"My head is spinning inside my cranium."<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=1h2iqp" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384423881ra/6873949.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>"I know.   <b>My Favorite Scene in the Entire Book in 3...2...1</b>

  <b>"...and at the first scrape of my nubbin against the rock-hard quad muscle of his thigh...</b>

</a><br><br>I'll be serious for a minute. I don't understand how anyone can enjoy writing like this. I struggled to get through. The writing was simplistic, repetitive, and amateur, the dialogue was silly, and the corn and cheese quotient went well beyond what anyone would count as acceptable. There were moments when Ms. Evans just abandoned any pretense at actual storytelling. There are at least four instances where the story almost completely self-destructs, and the book left me with more questions than it answered:<br><br>1. Did Brooke tear her ACL twice or break her ankle? <br>2. Is Pete's name Pete or Pedro? <br>3. Was the tension between Melanie and Riley because they <i>hadn't</i> slept together yet or because they <i>had</i>? <br>4. Did Melanie go home without us being told? One minute she's there, the next she's not. <br>5. Why did Remington, after an entire books' worth of silence about his feelings, go off for <i>five fucking pages</i> at the end about how much he lurves Brooke? <br>6. If a scorpion is an insect, why does Brooke refer to The Scorpion as "the reptile man"? <br>7. What the hell happened with Remington's parents? They showed up to see him, but he refused, and we never revisited <i>that</i> messy topic. <br>8. How did Nora manage to get rid of her tattoo and beat a cocaine addiction in a mere four weeks? <br>9. How is it possible for one man to spend a few million dollars a year? What is he spending all that money on? <br>10. He told Brooke he wants to be her "REAL". Her real <i>what</i>? Real vagey boyfriend? If so, mission accomplished.<br>11. Why was there <i>so much</i> poetic waxing about how utterly perfect and god-like and sexy and male and sweet and vulnerable and damaged and FUCK! WHY?! <br><br>Questions, questions, questions. The most burning question, however, is <b>how in the name of Blackbeard's glory hole has this gotten so many high ratings????</b><br><br>Word/Phrase Count: <br>"My sex" - 35<br>"Sex" - 35<br>"Sexy" - 60<br>"Wet" - 37<br>"Hot" - 80<br>"Eyes" - 384<br>"Scent" - 18<br>"Lust" - 26<br>"Gaze" - 50<br>"Heart" - 103<br>"Love" - 177<br>"Hair" - 90<br>"Beautiful" - 47<br>"My core" - 11<br>"Erection" - 20<br>"Fuck" - 36<br>"Fucks" - 6<br>"Fucking" - 75<br>"Delicious" - 13<br>"Mouth" - 144<br>"Clench" - 28<br>"Clenches" - 33<br>"Clenching" - 8<br>"Naked" - 26<br>"Liquid" - 16<br>"Heat" - 21<br>"Between my legs" - 16<br>"Hard" - 95<br>"Tight" - 25<br>"Sweat" - 13<br>"Male" - 25<br>"Inside me" - 58<br>"Muscle" - 21<br>"Muscles" - 52<br>"Nipples" - 21<br><b>"NUBBIN" - 2</b><br><br><br><br></span>

  <span id="freeText9688751866964072985" style="display:none">What. The. Fuck...<br /><br />I know everyone loves it, I can't hide that I <i> absolutely hated it</i> Editing again...turns out I have more to say. I can't let it go.<br /><br />DNF at 57% SPOILERS SPOILERS SPOILERS.<br /><br />I....No....I can't, it's just so bad. So bad.<br /><br />Basically the story is Brooke goes to watch a fight. Remy... A ummm man of few words- does that thing of seeing a girl once and being madly in love with her. This is the extent of his character...he wants Brooke and he fights, that's it.<br />So she gets hired as his muscle stretcher (???) and then a few days later goes away with Remy and his team. From the off there is sexual tension, if you consider clenching and twitching body parts tension.<br />At 57% this is all that has happened. I don't even think they had a full on conversation.<br /><br />When I started reading it, it was making me smile! I didn't <i> hate </i> it (that's a lie... I kind of did....but was not offended by it in any way) but I know this kind of book is hit and miss for me anyway. I was expecting to give it a 2 or 3 star rating....This was when I naively assumed the story progressed beyond "Wahhhh, why won't he have sex with me".<br /><br />I'm at a loss to be honest? Did I read the same book? I feel like I missed the point. I was perfectly willing to continue with the book until we started with the mental health thing. Just, no book, that's a cheap trick to use. A very sensitive cheap trick.<br />At that point we leaped from silly bad book, to potentially damaging incredibly insensitive book.<br /><br />For this to be used to add drama is huuuuugely offensive. To be told that he refuses to take medication because it's basically bad to put chemicals in your body and Brooke says "Sometimes the remedy is worse than the disease" What? Who says? I know a lot of people who have taken antidepressants- including myself (See I can admit that here, because IT'S NO BIG DEAL) and it is NOT an easy decision to take them. So for a book to have an alpha macho man be all "me no need drugs" is just wrong. Big fat effing wrong. If everybody with mental health issues was all 'take me as I am' some of them would have a severely impaired life, it's really irresponsible to say things like this. I can't even see how this can be remotely ok.<br /><br />He gets tranquilized at one point (Not even kidding), he is having a meltdown and he is tranquilized. Bipolar should not make him behave like the fucking Hulk, okay? No mention of therapy or other medication- we already know he's against this, but it's acceptable to be tranquilized? Who does that?! 'I have bipolar but I don't want to have treatment until I get 'speedy' (what?) and then my 'friends' tranquilize me and get me hookers so I can fuck the mental illness out of me.' Fuck off book.<br /><br />The clenching every single page....I didn't actually make it through the sex scene but if Remy managed to get inside that overly clenched woman I will be amazed. The woman must have a pelvic floor of steel.<br />I ended up with a nervous clenching twitch. It was just far too much, how can that go unnoticed? She clenches when he moves, talks, fights, eats, sleeps. Every.God.Damn.Thing. She reminds me of my cats when they are in season putting themselves on display like "pleeeeeease sexxxxx nowwwww"<br /><br />The scenting....is not logical, nobody scents, they smell. Brooke- Remy did not scent your hair, he smelled it. God damned book. He scents her more times than he talks to her. Also Brooke, your nipples are just that please don't call them breast tips, Oh my god.<br /><br />Magical writing like this.....<br /><blockquote>"My genetically induced mating instincts are at full attention, roaring inside me"<br /><br />"My sex muscles clench every time he hits his opponent" <br /><br />"My genes and DNA is a natural desire for healthy offspring, and with it comes a desperate desire to mate"<br /><br />"Maybe the cramp I thought I was getting in my ovaries was not cramp at all"<br /><br />"His hands clench on my hip, and my womb clenches with it so much it's painful and I almost whimper" </blockquote><br /><br />That's painful writing, man.<br /><br />I don't even know what to say other than what the actual shit is up with this book?!? <br /><br />'Genetically induced mating instincts' sounds like something my man would say to make me laugh whilst announcing he is horny. <br />Crampy ovaries? Clenching in response to being clenched? SEX MUSCLES?<br />I don't even know what to say.<br /><br />Not for me, no bloody way. This book is as far away from my favourites shelf as possible.</span>

<div id="review_691319296" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/691319296" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/691319296?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=na-experiment">na-experiment</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer691319296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3296145097188441113"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412193i/810513.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>I am conducting what I'm shelving as a "New Adult (NA) Experiment". I'm going to work my way through some of the popular New Adult books and see if I can weed out the crap and hopefully find some surprising gems. Here's hoping!</i><br/><br/>This was <u>bad</u>. I know there's a certain lack of believability in all romance novels, but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17617277.Real__Real___1_' title='Real (Real, #1) by Katy Evans' rel='nofollow noopener'>Real</a> took it to an all new level. There's not a single character here who's anything other than a caricature, rarely a piece of dialogue that's anything other than cringy, and definitel</span>
  <span id="freeText3296145097188441113" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412193i/810513.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>I am conducting what I'm shelving as a "New Adult (NA) Experiment". I'm going to work my way through some of the popular New Adult books and see if I can weed out the crap and hopefully find some surprising gems. Here's hoping!</i><br><br>This was <u>bad</u>. I know there's a certain lack of believability in all romance novels, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17617277.Real__Real___1_" title="Real (Real, #1) by Katy Evans" rel="nofollow noopener">Real</a> took it to an all new level. There's not a single character here who's anything other than a caricature, rarely a piece of dialogue that's anything other than cringy, and definitely never a description of the hormones and muscles in Brooke's body that sounds vaguely normal. On top of that, perhaps most damning of all, it was so so boring. I feel like I can sum this novel up simply as a 266-page description of Remington Tate's muscles.<br><br>I cannot deal with this level of physical description. Every time Remy walks into the room, speaks or breathes, Brooke's eyes are wandering over his perfect body, describing his perfect smile, just in case we didn't realise how he looks the last hundred times she's mentioned it. I find it amazing that there are four more books planned for this series! What can possibly happen? There's no plot beyond the adventures of Remy's rippling muscles. Books that offend me are more entertaining than this. At least I can see the root of the bestseller status with them - the intense (read: borderline abusive) relationships - but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17617277.Real__Real___1_" title="Real (Real, #1) by Katy Evans" rel="nofollow noopener">Real</a> is just brain-numbingly dull. Also, I'd like to know what's going on with this weird trend in NA. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17340050.Losing_Hope__Hopeless___2_" title="Losing Hope (Hopeless, #2) by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">Losing Hope</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15784909.This_Girl__Slammed___3_" title="This Girl (Slammed, #3) by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">This Girl</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15745950.Walking_Disaster__Beautiful___2_" title="Walking Disaster (Beautiful, #2) by Jamie McGuire" rel="nofollow noopener">Walking Disaster</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17830559.Remy__Real___3_" title="Remy (Real, #3) by Katy Evans" rel="nofollow noopener">Remy</a>... these books are all retellings of the first book from the POV of the guy. Why? I don't get the appeal. What's the point? Where's the tension, the suspense, in reading the story again?<br><br>Anyway, let's meet our protagonist. Brooke Dumas. The woman who is plucked out of a crowd of screaming female fans by Remington Tate. The woman who, despite having plenty of evidence to suggest Remy is obsessed with her and only her, still claims to be oblivious to his affections. <b>"Does he feel anything for me even remotely as strong as I do? There's this mean little part of me, the girl who broke her ACL and who failed to accomplish her dream, the girl who doesn't believe I can really have anything wonderful, makes me wonder if he really wants me at all."</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439314145ra/15821184.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>Moving on. The physical description of Remy is predictably pleasing: tall, dark hair, muscles, panty-dropping smile. And, of course, the character description of him predictably ruins it: angry, violent, arrogant, controlling. <b>"I can see he thinks he's the ultimate creation, and he seems to believe every woman here is his Eve, created from his ribcage for him to enjoy."</b> He sounds delightful. His sexiness evaporates further when he storms up to Brooke, grabs hold of her even though they've never met before, and this exchange happens:<br><br><b>"Your name," he growls, panting, his eyes wild on mine.<br>"Uh, Brooke."<br>"Brooke what?" he snaps out, his nostrils flaring.</b><br><br>Then he kisses her because he can and he wants to and he will. SEE-WANT-TAKE. It's so rude and presumptuous and I understand why some might find his confidence sexy, but I can't. And I'll tell you why.<br><br>A couple of years ago there was this guy I knew. A guy everyone knew, actually. He was incredibly good-looking but it was more than that too. He had an arrogant level of confidence that many women (and some men, for that matter) found attractive. Unless you know someone like him, I imagine it's hard to understand what he was like and the way people responded to him. He had such self-confidence that he would walk up to women he barely knew and sling his arm around their waist, lean in for a kiss on the lips. He did it so naturally, with such an air of certainty in the action that no one questioned it. Looking back, I can't believe no one questioned it. He kissed people, he touched them so casually, and any surprise the person initially had quickly disappeared in favour of delight that this hot guy had his arm around them and acted like it was the most natural thing in the world. Sometimes he went further. No one but him could get away with saying to someone "I'll see you later" with a promising wink and have them instantly agreeing without question. No one said no to him. Not even me, though thankfully I only kissed him. His way of behaving like everything he did was just the most obvious, most natural thing to do made it so no one thought to question it. Until one night this girl I only vaguely knew back then did question it. Actually, no, "question" is an insult to her, she told him a very firm "fuck off". And, whether because he was a bastard behind the pretty smile or because he genuinely couldn't believe someone meant NO when it was said to him, he didn't listen. <br><br>And it is books like this and characters like Remington that trigger such negative associations from me. Whenever I read about these men who are so used to getting a "yes" that they assume it's okay to grab someone's face because they want them, they make me uncomfortable. Their SEE-WANT-TAKE attitude makes me uneasy. No one is so beautiful and charming that it is impossible for anyone to say no to them. No one is above other people's right to decline.<br><br>Mel, Brooke's friend, particularly pissed me off with this. Remy is so gorgeous that she refuses to believe for a second that her friend might say no to him. Honestly, she is one of the worst friends in the world. What kind of friend gives your number to a guy without asking you, especially when she knows you probably wouldn't want her to? Brooke actually says to her: <b>"How could you give him my number? What do we even know about this man, Mel? Do you want me to end up murdered in some dark alley and my body parts tossed into some trash can?"</b><br><br>And what does Mel say? <b>"That's never going to happen to someone who's taken as many self-defense classes as you."</b> I can't even deal with the stupid in that statement. And then Mel says this gem: <b>"Remington Tate may have a bad rap, but he's sexier than sin, Brooke. Yes, he was banned for poor conduct because he's a naughty, wicked boy."</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380432556ra/868972.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, let's get onto the "sexy" aspect of this novel. Sometimes these NA novels do that fairly successfully even if they fail at everything else. But, I swear, Brooke's descriptions remind me of David Attenborough describing mating rituals of some mammal or other. It's just bad, cringe-worthy writing. Like this: <b>"I'm familiar enough with the subject to know that wired into my genes and DNA is a natural desire for healthy offspring, and with it comes a desperate urge to just full out mate with whoever I deem is the prime male of my species. I have never in my life met a man before who sparks up my crazy mating instincts like him."</b><br><br>And, oh my god, the <i>clenching</i>. The author loves the word "clench". If Remy's muscles aren't clenching, then it's Brooke's vagina. Every page someone is clenching. Hands clench, teeth clench, abs clench, vaginas clench, facial muscles clench. Things I didn't even know could clench somehow clench. This is from the second page: <b>"My sex muscles clench every time he hits his opponent."</b> Seriously, girl, you oughtta get that checked out. And you especially oughtta get this checked out: <b>"Maybe the cramp I thought I was getting in my ovaries was not cramp at all."</b><br><br>o_O Ladies, do you all have this problem? Because, frankly, I'm not experiencing this confusion over whether it's cramps or horniness. Just sayin'. There's a whole bunch of eyebrow-raising phrases like this...<br><br><b>"He keeps making sexual foreplay to my ear."</b><br><br><b>"Remy inhales me."</b>... <b>"Remy scented me."</b> I think this means he's sniffing her. Mmm 'kay. <br><br><b>"Why won't you take me, Remington?"<br>"Because I want you too much."</b> - Give me a break.<br><br><b>"Remington, whose jaw seems even squarer than I remember, like it's made of the most gorgeous, most priceless piece of granite the world has ever found."</b><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17617277.Real__Real___1_" title="Real (Real, #1) by Katy Evans" rel="nofollow noopener">Real</a>, in short, is just annoying, boring and poorly written. I have completely exhausted myself and I hope I never again hear anything about Remy's control issues and Brooke's "breast tips" and "nubbin". FYI, Brooke, that's your nipples and clitoris.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3296145097188441113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_586303856" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/586303856" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/586303856?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer586303856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17375067770196670319"><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417042i/824379._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b> Please don't lynch me!!<br/><br/>I'm a little scared to say this given all the passionate fans of this book but, if I'm going to be honest, I just wasn't feeling it. </b><br/><br/>I mean, I get it. I totally get why so many readers loved it. It had a hot Alpha (somewhat damaged) hero, boat loads of steam and all, plus he was a fighter (gotta love the bad boys, right?) but... I just honestly barely felt anything while reading. I also had several issues with some of the content and then found the ending absolutely predi</span>
  <span id="freeText17375067770196670319" style="display:none"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417042i/824379._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> Please don't lynch me!!<br><br>I'm a little scared to say this given all the passionate fans of this book but, if I'm going to be honest, I just wasn't feeling it. </b><br><br>I mean, I get it. I totally get why so many readers loved it. It had a hot Alpha (somewhat damaged) hero, boat loads of steam and all, plus he was a fighter (gotta love the bad boys, right?) but... I just honestly barely felt anything while reading. I also had several issues with some of the content and then found the ending absolutely predictable. Nothing ever surprised me or make my heart race so ... I just don't think this story was for me.<br><br>I know a LOT of readers loved it though, it's been getting so many 5 star ratings, so I know that in many people's eyes it's got something special and I fully respect that, I guess I just personally couldn't connect to it.<br><br>REAL follows the story of Brooke and Remy. Remy was the champion boxer who every woman just lost their heads over. He was hot, dangerous, and unbeatable in the ring. When Brooke's friend drags her to one of his fights, they have a chance encounter and from that moment on are hooked on each other.<br><br>But when she was called to his hotel room after the fight, the last thing she expected was to be offered a job to tour with them. Brooke specialized in athlete rehab therapy and Remy wanted her there to help him with his training and after his fights. Or so he says. What he was really looking for is something "real". A real connection. Not to Remington "Riptide" Tate, but to him, Remy. She agreed, and their story began.<br><br>I had several issues with the story but I'm just going to just list a few of the main ones then leave it at that so that you can get a feel for what bothered me.<br><br>My first issue was their connection, or lack of. For me, it was too much, too soon. The entire story was told from Brooke's perspective and I just felt there was SO much focus (right from like page 2) on how hot she was for him every time she even saw him that I felt there was no time spent on actually building a real connection between them.<br><br>My second issues was the repetitiveness of both the scenes and certain words. There was a lot of clenching, muscle bulging, drenching etc. I'm not usually one to nit pick, but the word 'clench' was used over 70 times in the book. That's a lot of clenching. And it began on page 3. Another term that I began to tire of was 'speedy'. Now the hero was bi-polar. And (I'll address my issues regarding that next) but whenever he had an episode, they called it him going 'speedy' and I just got tired of the word. And just in general, a lot of the wording really made me mentally 'trip' while reading. Here's an example of the kind of thing that just didn't work for me.<br><br><blockquote> <i> "Tonight we’re both naked and deliciously entangled, and my sexy blue-eyed lion now seems content to have petted me for a long while, until I feel groomed down to my bones." </i>
</blockquote><br>Ok, next, about him being bi-polar. I won't give the details because I don't want to spoil them, but basically, everything regarding the way his medical condition was a bit of a stretch to the point that it wasn't even remotely believable. I felt that, if the author was going to use that plot element, she should have use it accurately. I normally try to look past this sort of thing but it really bothered me here because it was referenced several time and there was just no way it was remotely plausible. His condition was described as some sort of gene switch that flicked back and forth and could also be determined by looking at his eyes which switched from blue to black if he had an 'episode'. His eye color chance was also linked to this gene switch. In a paranormal story, sure, I'd buy it. In a real life story, no way.<br><br>And finally, I predicted the ending from about a half way into the story. To a tee. So there was no adrenaline rush or anything because I just knew exactly what was going to happen.<br><br>I thought this book had great potential. I liked Remy a lot as a character and I even think that in a different book, I could have maybe fully fallen in love with him. His back-story made my heart ache and it set him up wonderfully as a damaged/tortured hero and I totally understood where he was coming from in terms of wanting to find something 'real' in a relationship.<br><br><blockquote> <i> “Why’d you want to have sex with me? To have a fucking adventure? What was I supposed to be? Your one-night-fucking stand? I’m every woman’s adventure, damn you, and I don’t want to be yours. I want to be your fucking REAL. You get that?"<br><br>“I want this. Very badly.” He nuzzles my nose with his. “I’m trying not to fuck it up, all right?” </i> </blockquote><br>See? Now that stuff is swoony! And the way I look at it is this. I liked Remy. I really did. What I didn't like was everything surrounding him - including the heroine, which sucked because the story was told from her perspective. But, the result was that it made it harder for me to connect to the book as a whole (including Remy).<br><br>I mean, there were a few awwww moments, a few really gorgeous lines, and a few moments where I felt the hint of a 'spark' in their connection but those moments were brief and didn't last long enough to sway me into fully liking the book.<br><br>I fully respect that many people loved this book, it just really wasn't for me.<br><br><b> 3.5 - 4 stars for Remy's character. <br>2 stars for the rest of the book. </b><br><br><img width="100%" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1363442697l/17617277.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17375067770196670319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_585079306" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/585079306" />
    <a title="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8524618-angie---angie-s-dreamy-reads"><img alt="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578074503p2/8524618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/585079306?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" href="/user/show/8524618-angie---angie-s-dreamy-reads">Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8524618-angie---angie-s-dreamy-reads?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer585079306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer175935054740959701">***WARNING THIS IS A SWOONTASTIC, RAVING, FANATICAL REVIEW!!! READ AT YOUR OWN RISK!***<br/><br/><b>5 STARS ...NO WAY!!!!!!! THIS BOOK IS A MILLION STAR BOOK!!! FAN-FREAKING-TASTC</b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>"When I take you, you'll be mine," he says, a soft promise in my ear. He slides his thumb along my jaw, then gently kisses my earlobe. "You need to be certain." His eyes are so hot that I'm on fire with the lust in them, and the word "mine" makes the empty place between my legs swell with longing. "I want you to know me first, an</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText175935054740959701" style="display:none">***WARNING THIS IS A SWOONTASTIC, RAVING, FANATICAL REVIEW!!! READ AT YOUR OWN RISK!***<br /><br /><b>5 STARS ...NO WAY!!!!!!! THIS BOOK IS A MILLION STAR BOOK!!! FAN-FREAKING-TASTC</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"When I take you, you'll be mine," he says, a soft promise in my ear. He slides his thumb along my jaw, then gently kisses my earlobe. "You need to be certain." His eyes are so hot that I'm on fire with the lust in them, and the word "mine" makes the empty place between my legs swell with longing. "I want you to know me first, and then, I want you to let me know if you still want me to take you." -Remy</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>AHHHHHHHHHHHHHH!!!!!!! REMY...REMY...REMY...REMY!! </b><i><br />**be still my beating heart**</i><br /><br /><b>HOLY SHIT!!!!</b> This book has me feeling consumed from the inside out. Remy and Brooke have taken over every part of my heart. I can’t even begin to explain the emotional amazingness that it is. How do I describe a book that's indescribable? How do I put into words just what this book has created, stirred and induced within me? It’s without a doubt <b>THE BEST</b> book I have read this year. It’s made me want to go back and re rate all the other books that I’ve read because next to the feelings that this has produced, they can’t even compare. If you’re thinking about reading this book <b>DO IT NOW</b>. I know you have an epic TBR and I know the choice of books out there is <b>HUGE</b> but <b>THIS BOOK</b>, <b>THIS MASTERPIECE</b>, that’s packed with sexual tension, palpable emotion, sweat inducing sizzle and a love story that will stick with you, will become your new favorite book without a doubt.<br /><br />When I fall in love with a book everything in me wants to scream it from the mountain top. Everything in me wants to share the way it made me feel. I want to share this feeling with <b>YOU</b> because it’s euphoric!!! The high it’s created in me is immense and intense. You know that feeling of being on cloud nine? That feeling of not being able to think about anything else? That feeling of being <b>IN</b> the book? When you experience something <b>SO, SO, SO</b> special!! That’s the way this book will make you feel.<br /><br />I’m <b>COMPLETELY</b> obsessed with these characters!!!<br /><br /><b>
  <u>What the books about? Here’s the blurb:</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>A fallen boxer.<br />A woman with a broken dream.<br />A competition…<br /><br />He even makes me forget my name. One night was all it took, and I forgot everything and anything except the sexy fighter in the ring who sets my mind ablaze and my body on fire with wanting…<br /><br />Remington Tate is the strongest, most confusing man I’ve ever met in my life.<br /><br />He’s the star of the dangerous underground fighting circuit, and I’m drawn to him as I’ve never been drawn to anything in my life. I forget who I am, what I want, with just one look from him. When he’s near, I need to remind myself that I am strong–but he is stronger. And now it’s my job to keep his body working like a perfect machine, his taut muscles primed and ready to break the bones of his next opponents . . .<br /><br />But the one he’s most threatening to, now, is me.<br /><br />I want him. I want him without fear. Without reservations.<br /><br />If only I knew for sure what it is that he wants from me? </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Remy is <b>F&amp;@#NG</b> hot!! I swear his name alone cause panties to combust, dampen and melt. He’s hot...ladies. <b>HOT, HOT, HOT, HOT</b>. I can’t even rate the hotness. Think Travis Maddox times 1 million. Yeah, yeah I know that’s a huge comparison but Remy is all <b>MAN</b>! He’s alpha, primal, sex on a stick, intense, sweet, possessive. He’s <b>EVERYTHING, EVERYTHING</b> you could ever want!! But you wanna know the best part about him? His tender heart!! He has a heart of gold. OH.MY.GOD...I can't even tell you. He's so freaking incredible with Brooke. The love he has for that woman is <b>UNIMAGINABLE!</b> It's the <b>BEST</b> thing ever!! Ugh...here I go swooning again. I can't stop myself! <br /><br /><b>I LOVE HIM! <br />I LOVE<br />LOVE<br />LOVE<br />LOVE<br />H.I.M!!! </b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>He smells my neck and then buzzes the back of my ear, and whispers into me, "You're my mate, and I've claimed you." - Remy</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Brooke see's Remy and it’s LUST and something even deeper at first sight. I swear the connection is <b>INSTANT!</b> Now I know we aren't all a fan of insta love right?! Well this my fellow readers is a case of insta love done right! It's <b>PERFECT</b>. Brooke see's Remy, the spark is there, and then she's offered a job with him, takes it and the sexy, steamy anticipation of them connecting and falling in love has you sitting on the edge of your seat. It's so freaking good!!<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"My heart pounds when I reach out, my hand quaking as a touch the top of his head. "Have you ever been anyone's?" I ask, a feathery whisper in the bedroom. He lists his head to mine, and I want him so bad I feel consumed inside, like he's already possessed my soul, and now my soul aches for him to possess my body."-Brooke</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Brooke is one of the best chicks in a book I've read. <b>EVERYTHING</b> she thought, felt or saw I experienced! I loved her, never got annoyed with her and completely <b>ADORED</b> every moment of reading about her. Her feelings for Remy where the same feelings that I felt. I fell in love with him in the exact same way she did! She's the girl that we want to be. Independent but real. How many times do we read books and HATE or get annoyed at the female lead?! Too many but Brooke is a girl in her own league. You will <b>LOVE</b> her. <br /><br />Together Remy and Brooke <b>DEFINE</b> sexual anticipation. God they are a walking, talking ball of hotness. They are so fantastic together. Think Kellan and Kiera, Abbi and Travis, Ana and Christian amazing!! They’re just brilliant as a couple. They complement each other, were made for each other...swoon, swoon, swoon!! The relationship is so sexual <b>BUT</b> it’s more than that!! They don’t just want each other, they <b>NEED, LIVE and BREATH</b>each other. It’s the love we dream about. <br /><br /><b>AHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH</b><br /><br />It’s what every girl wants. I want it. Damn....what a book. Seriously <b>WHAT.AN.AMAZING.BOOK!!</b> It’s so flipping good. It's a love story on crack. It's going to be addictive the moment you pick it up. <b>TRUST ME</b> this book is going to be all you'll think about. It's all consuming. So what are you waiting for...<b>GO, GO, GO!! BUY THE BOOK!!</b> I'll even put the links at the end of this review. It's going to <b>ROCK YOUR WORLD!</b></span>

<div id="review_580075794" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/580075794" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/580075794?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>

<div id="review_593448585" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/593448585" />
    <a title="Rachel (BAVR)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6303796-rachel-bavr"><img alt="Rachel (BAVR)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396635700p2/6303796.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/593448585?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel (BAVR)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel (BAVR)" href="/user/show/6303796-rachel-bavr">Rachel (BAVR)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=blame-bavr">blame-bavr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=my-eyes-my-eyes">my-eyes-my-eyes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=things-that-don-t-make-sense">things-that-don-t-make-sense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=worst-person-ever-heroine">worst-person-ever-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=worst-person-ever-hero">worst-person-ever-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=angst-city">angst-city</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=rape-is-not-love">rape-is-not-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=attack-of-the-mary-sues">attack-of-the-mary-sues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6303796-rachel-bavr?shelf=constanticrap">constanticrap</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer593448585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16926405232560743915">Nothing in the world could have prepared me for this book. It’s too much and too little and too fucking <b>bad</b> for my brain to wrap itself around. I like romance. Really, I do. But books like <i>Real</i> are twisting the romance genre to a place where the phrases “pussy lips” and “fucks my ear” are becoming the norm, and I can’t with that. I can’t. <br/><br/>And how about these “hot alpha heroes” the writers have been cranking out lately? What a bunch of assholes. Just empty, pointless shells of rudimentary DNA and</span>
  <span id="freeText16926405232560743915" style="display:none">Nothing in the world could have prepared me for this book. It’s too much and too little and too fucking <b>bad</b> for my brain to wrap itself around. I like romance. Really, I do. But books like <i>Real</i> are twisting the romance genre to a place where the phrases “pussy lips” and “fucks my ear” are becoming the norm, and I can’t with that. I can’t. <br><br>And how about these “hot alpha heroes” the writers have been cranking out lately? What a bunch of assholes. Just empty, pointless shells of rudimentary DNA and 0% body fat. After another one of my forays into the New Adult world, my AXEL! experience, I wrote an ode to the New Alpha. However, after reading about Remy in <i>REAL</i>, it seems that my ode was incomplete. <br><br>With no further ado, BAVR’s Ode to the New Alpha: Remy Edition…<br><br><blockquote>He's hot, ripped, and hung like a horse.<br>His dick slices through granite and punches ten sharks. <br>He likes a girl with a vagina that can gush like a geyser <br>and HATES any man who dares look sideways at her. <br>His sperm are like ninjas that make dragon babies. <br>He may speak like a child but fucks like 8 porn stars. <br>The New Alpha makes good girls fantasize about douchebags. <br>Who needs good characterization when - blah, blah, blah - <b>12 pack</b>?<br><br>Hark! None of these douchebags prepared us for Remy,<br>who licks like a lion and plays with his semen. <br>His spiky black hair and his pants worn <i>that way</i><br>make women have orgasms in public arenas.<br>He speaks through a series of grunts and gruff growls<br>but all of his street cred comes from his iPod – GOO GOO DOLLS!<br>They say that his cock moves faster than the speed of light.<br>There it is, behind you! You’re pregnant now, slut!</blockquote><br><br>So, whatever, the moment has arrived to review this masterpiece. It’s time to stop being polite and start getting REAL. The REAL World: Brooke’s Vagina.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418080ra/827553.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You know what makes books like <i>Real</i> most insufferable to me? They’re shallow. The plot of this is just a partially evaporated puddle of piss in the desert. There is no reality to “Real,” no substance. It is what it fucking is, and that is a poorly crafted self-insert fic with squicky sex. <br><br>Our narrator is Brooke Dumas, a sports rehabilitation specialist (or in simpler terms, a “stretcher”)who swore off men after hurting her leg in the Olympic trial. Her vagina could drown a small village if a hot six-pack walked by. <br><br>The first time she sees Remy:<br><i>My panties are soaked, and my pulse has gone haywire.</i><br><br>When Remy talks:<br><i>My thighs go watery when the answering voice slides across the shell of my ear, both velvet and chillingly hard.</i><br><br>At seeing acts of violence:<br><i>My sex muscles clench every time he hits an opponent.</i><br><br>Brooke’s sex muscles always clench. I’m surprised Remy never got his peen stuck in there, to be honest. The other thing we have to know about Brooke is that she doesn’t know what “literally” means. This is important because correct usage of words is KIND OF THE WHOLE POINT ABOUT BOOKS. <br><br>For example, Brooke can’t sprint anymore because she hurt her leg and WAH, WAH, WAH, that’s her tragic backstory. Then she thinks this:<br><i>I want to go crazy. Bungee. Sprint again, even if only in a literal sense.</i><br><br>And then Brooke implies that she may be a dragon:<br><i>There is, literally, a ball of fire in my throat, and I can’t even swallow my saliva.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418080ra/827554.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Brooke uses words like a handless man wearing a blindfold uses a hammer – blindly and with no discernible precision. There are several very boring passages where she pretends to be all smart and shit by using anatomical terms to describe Remy’s glistening deltoids or whatever, but all of that “I R TEH SMARTZ” dies when she thinks things like this:<br><br><i>My head is spinning inside my cranium.</i><br><br>Time to submit that phrase to thingsthatcan’thappen.com. <br><br>Oh, and this:<br><br><i>For the past four evenings, he’s come get me from my room and carry me back to his, and on this last one, I even stayed the full day.</i><br><br>Seriously. Editing is not evil, writers. Give it a try.<br><br>So, anyway, Brooke is insufferable. The time that she doesn’t spend ruminating over Remy’s “perfection” and hot penis is spent feeling like she’s the cat’s meow for being the cure for Remy’s Bipolar episodes and beating out all the whores and sluts for his sexxors and love. <br><br>And then there’s Remington “Riptide” Tate, the PERFECT and UNBEATABLE underground fighter with the SOUL OF A LION. Or whatevs. Remy has “people,” and all that these people basically do is pay off the hotel and wait staffs when Remy goes manic and destroys shit and shoot him full of tranquilizers when he gets violent outside of the ring. <br><br>Yes, in REAL, Remy is bipolar, and it’s insultingly fetishized. A sensitive, nuanced issue like Bipolar Disorder deserves a far smarter book than REAL to pay it the proper respect. Brooke just fucking loves it when he goes manic, mostly because he gets really, really horny, and also because she likes to feel needed. Aside from the tranquilizers, Remy will NOT take medication for his very dangerous condition. Because this is real, you see, and making the true love with a man who could snap and kill you without remembering it in the morning IS TOTALLY NORMAL. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/338573.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Brooke doesn’t give a shit about any of this, of course, because thinking about Remy’s mental illness in a thoughtful way wouldn’t make her wet. In fact, if this book mentions something other than how perfect, hot, glistening, hard, strong Remy is, it only lasts for a couple of paragraphs. Because we can’t tear our attention away from how HAWT this empty shell of a character with his Tragic Backstory of the Week is, can we? Note to authors: If you describe your hero as “perfect,” YOU’RE DOING CHARACTERIZATION WRONG. <br><br><i>But come on, Rachel</i>, you say, thinking I seem like a huge bitch for being mean to this book. <i>The sex has to be good. Right? RIGHT?</i><br><br><i>His expression is tense, ravenous, so hot as he scrapes his finger deep into my channel. "Do you want me inside you?"</i><br><br>WHY IS HE SCRAPING INSIDE OF HER VAGINA?!<br><br><i>"Sticky?" he asks in a gruff manner, bending his head and licking my shoulder as he pushes his semen back inside with one finger.</i><br><br>I SEE SO MANY INFECTIONS RESULTING FROM THIS. WHAT THE FUCK ARE YOU DOING?<br><br><i>”When I get you in bed, I’m going to scrub you raw with my fucking tongue until there’s nothing anywhere on you from him. Only me. Only <b>me</b>.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418080ra/827555.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’m finished with this. The secondary characters and sequel bait aren’t even worth mentioning because I know Evans will make them have all kinds of icky semen covered sex in future books. As for Remy and Brooke’s future book, I won’t be reading it. Because this first book is basically the same shallow thought on repeat for a couple hundred pages mixed with some very rough writing, I don’t see how the second one will be any different. Obviously, there’s a target audience for this kind of book, but I’m not in it. Not even close. <br><br>Read my status updates for more squicky excerpts. You won’t enjoy a minute of it. <br><br>Also: Read my buddy reader Karla’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/704952707" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a> for some more fleshed-out thoughts that I don’t currently have the emotional capacity to handle. &gt;:D<br><br>One more quote before I go:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Do you like what I do to you ... with this...?" When he slides his sweatpants off, I'm fainting with the sight of ten Remington's butts in the reflections behind him, his powerful legs from behind, his narrow waist and broad shoulders.<br><br>And his cock, standing before me.<br><br>I've just died.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>And a visual representation of how I feel about this book:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380418080i/827556.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="16926405232560743915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer585395964" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2030109251917734510">Oh Katy Evens, you made me laugh so hard today. Your brilliant satire on the state of modern women in their early 20s is an insightful critique of the unabashed shallowness and anti-feminist behavior spawned by such books as "Fifty Shades of Gray." Your tongue-in-cheek references to pretentious pop culture icons, and your commentary on the recent abundance of literary misogynists was riveting. The way you crafted your prose eloquently showed how hyperbole and hyper-erotic imagery can be used to </span>
  <span id="freeText2030109251917734510" style="display:none">Oh Katy Evens, you made me laugh so hard today. Your brilliant satire on the state of modern women in their early 20s is an insightful critique of the unabashed shallowness and anti-feminist behavior spawned by such books as "Fifty Shades of Gray." Your tongue-in-cheek references to pretentious pop culture icons, and your commentary on the recent abundance of literary misogynists was riveting. The way you crafted your prose eloquently showed how hyperbole and hyper-erotic imagery can be used to destroy the innate sensuality of a character. Bravo for such a smart, funny, poignant work of art. It... <br /> <br />Wait, what?<br /><br />This ISN'T a joke? <br /><br />No way, are you serious? This is for real? <br /><br />No, I don't believe you. There is no way she meant some of these lines non-ironically. No way. <br /><br />You think so, do you? Well, let me see what other people thought.<br /><br />Holy crap, people like this book?! Like seriously? They liked this slut-shaming, stereotype-reinforcing, panty-soaking, womb-clenching drivel? Huh...<br /> <br />Well, a round of applause for those of you who made it through this book. I only got through 25% before I gave up. Maybe it improves... and maybe pigs have started flying and bunnies have started conversing and unicorns have starting lobbying for some<i> respect</i> among the supernatural animal community. All I know is that I'm significantly dumber than I was when I woke up this morning. <br /><br />**Copy provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review** </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14367119107350545443"><b>Review FINALLY posted.</b><br/><br/><b>3 to 3 1/2 stars</b><br/><br/>Looks like I'm in the minority here. I liked this book but didn't love it. <br/><br/><i>Real</i> intrigued me, captivated me, overwhelmed me, baffled me, and annoyed me. <b>It has to be the single most repetitive and overly sexualized book I have ever read. And that says something!</b> Still, I couldn't put it down, so I guess that says something, too. <br/><br/>Overall, my biggest issues with this book—other than Booke's excessive babbling about how she looses control over her nether region</span>
  <span id="freeText14367119107350545443" style="display:none"><b>Review FINALLY posted.</b><br /><br /><b>3 to 3 1/2 stars</b><br /><br />Looks like I'm in the minority here. I liked this book but didn't love it. <br /><br /><i>Real</i> intrigued me, captivated me, overwhelmed me, baffled me, and annoyed me. <b>It has to be the single most repetitive and overly sexualized book I have ever read. And that says something!</b> Still, I couldn't put it down, so I guess that says something, too. <br /><br />Overall, my biggest issues with this book—other than Booke's excessive babbling about how she looses control over her nether regions (the girl's a dripping faucet) and is all agog whenever she sees or is around Remington—is the fact that I never felt like I truly knew who Remington was as a character. I know this sounds strange but I loved him without knowing why I loved him. It was an odd feeling and one that left me somewhat discombobulated by the end of the book. <br /><br />While this particular story didn't fully work for me–I found the heroine annoying and somewhat one-dimensional–I can see why others loved this book. It's an addictive read with an elusive hero that impossible not to love or swoon over. <br /></span>

<div id="review_704952707" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/704952707" />
    <a title="Karla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2846441-karla"><img alt="Karla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537371209p2/2846441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/704952707?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karla" href="/user/show/2846441-karla">Karla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2846441-karla?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer704952707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9698662093101920074"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434523i/877065.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>More later. -__-<br/><br/>***<br/><br/><i>OK, here goes....</i><br/><br/>I'm not gonna lie: when I see an overwhelming fuckton of 5 star squee attached to something labeled as "New Adult," I have a proportionately overwhelming desire to read it and see if it is indeed <i>all that</i>. Since I'm a bastard person at heart, I think you can guess what the inevitable result usually is.<br/><br/>But this...this, my friends, was a colossal shitburger of epic proprtions.<br/><br/>There ain't no subjective about it. Objectively, it was bad. Objectively, it was one of</span>
  <span id="freeText9698662093101920074" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434523i/877065.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>More later. -__-<br><br>***<br><br><i>OK, here goes....</i><br><br>I'm not gonna lie: when I see an overwhelming fuckton of 5 star squee attached to something labeled as "New Adult," I have a proportionately overwhelming desire to read it and see if it is indeed <i>all that</i>. Since I'm a bastard person at heart, I think you can guess what the inevitable result usually is.<br><br>But this...this, my friends, was a colossal shitburger of epic proprtions.<br><br>There ain't no subjective about it. Objectively, it was bad. Objectively, it was one of the absolute worst entries in the New Adult genre that has met to wide acclaim. "Oh, but surely," you might say, "<i>Fifty Shades of Grey</i> is infinitely worse in, well, <i>everything!</i>" And you'd probably be right since <i>Real</i> at least has the good sense to be less than half the length of FSoG, but there is still a lot of <b>Worst. Writing. Evar.</b> and a lot of hair-pulling offensiveness packed in those pages. It gets its own little trophy.<br><br>I know that this is the author's first book and it's bound to be of iffy quality. (Self-pubbed + New Adult practically makes that a given.) I <i>know</i> that it's a labor of love and the author loves her characters and loves everything they say and do and the manuscript was probably never seen by anyone willing (or able) to give it a good going-over. <b>I GET IT.</b> But that still doesn't mean that this saga of Brooke Dumas and Remington Tate didn't suck huge, hairy donkey balls.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434523ra/877066.gif" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Yeah, I should work on that...<b>later.</b></i><br><br>One recurring <s>excuse</s> comment I see regarding self-pubbed romances like this is that even if the writing "needs work," at least there's "a good story." To which I ask: What story? Excuse me, was there a plot here? OK, here was the plot:<br><br>Brooke Dumas sees Remington Tate at an "underground" fighting match and he sees her and he gets hard and she gets wet. He offers her a job as his "stretcher" and she takes it. He's hard; she's wet. Brooke finds out her little sister Nora is the druggie ho of Remy's archnemesis of the ring and wants to help her escape. Brooke also discovers Remy's bipolar and doesn't take meds but has a routine where he goes manic and gets jabbed in the neck with sedatives like he's a rampaging rhino or something. It makes her all protective/nurturing/wet. Remy goes real manic over dumb shit. Nora's rescued. Hardness and wetness ensue. The End.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434523ra/877067.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm not simplifying things and leaving out details. That really is it. <b>That is it.</b> Because you want to know what the majority of the book is?<br><br>Brooke fapping to every single inch of Remy. Every little body part. Over and over. There is not a single Remy-centric noun that isn't attached to at least one adjective, usually with an absolute modifier attached to it (namely: <i>perfect</i>). <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434523i/877068.jpg" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>He's got the perfectest gravity-defying flufferbuttle EVER.</i><br><br>The bluest eyes. The muscleyest muscles. The tightest butt. The strongest jaw. Arms, legs, thighs, hands, fingers, eyelashes, and cock. Everrrrrything. Hard, long, thick, slender, tanned. The most. The best. Constant and relentless.<br><br>And then there's the pages upon pages upon <i>pages</i> of Brooke commenting on how wet and clenchy she is. When they actually start fucking, it gets even worse.<br><br>The writing is such an endless wallow in teenager-in-love-with-high-school-jock that I ping-ponged between<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434523ra/877069.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434523ra/877070.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>IDK. There's really no place to go but up, and someone of her age who wants to sell fiction should learn that the basics of storytelling do not begin and end with how hot your hero is. Having your heroine say it over and over don't make it so. And it certainly doesn't constitute a plot.<br><br>I don't know if the motivation or incentive to improve is there since this execrable first offering was so hella popular and got picked up by Simon &amp; Schuster. I read the original edition and a glance at the "professional" product shows some of the worst grammatical mistakes still intact so...another victory for cheap cashing in by the Big Six. I can't believe they're charging nearly 10 bucks for what is basically the author's self-insert wish fulfillment fantasy porn from the darkest recesses of her laptop, written by her inner 13-year old who has confused porn with good smut. (Stuffing semen back in? That's hot in what fucking universe?? Maybe Larry Flynt wouldn't give you the side eye for that. <i>Maybe.</i>)<br><br>Apart from the embarrassingly awful writing, the use of manic depression as a cheap dwama ploy is understandably offensive. I don't have much to say on the specifics since there are others who have first-hand experience with more of substance to say about it. I'm not bipolar and I don't know anyone intimately that suffers from it (that I know of, anyway) so it's not in the realm of my expertise. I get moody, have a good cry, and get over myself. Yeah, you don’t need meds for <i>that</i>, but Remy’s problem? He needs a lithium drip. The author trotting out the whole issue solely to make Remy a woobie and Brooke want to kiss and cuddle him back into his real eye color is...words fail.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434523ra/877073.gif" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Brooke opines that Remy's refusal to take meds is understandable because the cure can be worse than the disease, and what can help his bipolarity is teh healing sexxors with the One True Vagina, I called BULLSHIT and gave this book the salute it deserves:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434523ra/877074.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even though I feel like I've been going on forever, I've only skimmed the surface of what I hated about it. The fault lies in the fact that rarely did a page go by where I <i>didn't</i> groan, facepalm, shake my head, roll my eyes, etc. Brooke's inner dialogue, the flat secondary characters, the series bait, Brooke's speshul snowflakery, the cornball "red roses from Remy" with Hollywood crowd clap (I still lost it right thar despite knowing allllllll about it beforehand), the euphemism "wet little kitten" (holy shit, the LOLZ), the biochemistry and muscle group infodumps, the stupid playlist-sharing theme with ponderous explanations of <b>THE MEANING OF THE LYRICS ZOMG</b>, and the <i>hilarious</i> demonizing of <b>BENNY THE SCORPION</b> into something that looks like The Toxic Avenger with the morals of Satan, simply because he baited the easily-baited Remy once upon a manic time. Go wish him into the cornfield, Brooke. He's a very bad man!<br><br>It took no time at all for her to be his wet, clenching avenger, unquestioning practically everything about him and engaging in bar fights with his foes simply because he's so hot and he makes her wet. Love for all time? I so didn't see it. All I could see was wall-to-wall physical reaction and body obsessing. Shallow shallow <i>SHALLOW.</i> For a book that spent nearly its entirety in Brooke's brain, the actual substance wouldn't fill a thimble.<br><br>And what was up with her sexual experience? She goes from losing her virginity at the Olympic tryouts (athletes get horny before showtime, yo) and swearing off men after her life-destroying injury at said tryouts (what one has to do with the other is anybody's guess), to being able to deep throat Remy's massive, one of a kind, world record-breaking cock in one go. It was almost as if Brooke was some changeable stand-in for whatever fantasy was at hand. Hmmm..... These placeholder heroines are the fucking <i>pits</i>, y'all.<br><br>And the author's going to redo this story from Remy's POV? Ugh.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434523ra/877075.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let me guess: He's going to be hard for her ALL THE TIME and scared that he'll hurt her during one of his "black" and "speedy" phases and those two things will be on an endless fucking loop. And that's all the insight we'll get. There. I just saved you 10 bucks.<br><br>0 stars. I've read worse books ("worse" in that there weren't nearly as many lulz as what Evans unintentionally dished out and being bored is a mortal sin IMO), but I have never read a more embarrassingly puerile piece of tripe by someone old enough to know better.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434523i/877076._SY540_.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>This was a Buddy Read with Rachel, whose excellent review can be found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/593448585" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. You won't want to miss her</i> "Ode to the New Alpha," <i>an ongoing project to serenade the most knuckle-dragging lamebrains among New Adult heroes.</i></span>

Damn you Remy, you made me ugly cry!<br/><br/><b>
  I’m every woman’s adventure, damn you, and I don’t want to be yours. I want to be your fucking REAL. You get that? If I fuck you, I want you to belong to me. To be mine. I want you to give yourself to me—not Riptide</b></span>

Damn you Remy, you made me ugly cry!<br><br><b>

</b><br><br>I have read and loved so very many books but, every now and then, a book comes along that stands head and shoulders above all the others, a book that simply takes your breath away, steals your ability to concentrate on anything else, a book that completely consumes you and owns you. THIS is that book. It’s such a soulful. beautiful and emotional story and even now, when I close my eyes, I’m right back with Brooke &amp; Remy. Nothing is forgotten – this book will stay with me forever.<br><br>Brooke first sees Remy at an underground boxing fight. She’s been dragged there by her best friend Mel and she’s not prepared for what is about to happen. As Remington “Riptide” Tate takes to the ring their eyes lock and something passes between them – time stands still and they share an instant and unshakable connection. At this point, just a few pages in, I knew I was going to love this book. I knew it was special and even told my friend who I was sitting next to at the time. She gave me a quizzical look and said ‘What? After just two pages?’ and I just nodded. I knew instinctively this book was going to be exceptional.<br><br>Remy is a fallen boxer now competing in an underground circuit. He’s in prime physical shape – he’s pure masculinity and raw beast, sex on a stick, a six-foot-plus tower of testosterone. He’s tall, dark with piercing blue eyes – every girl’s dream and he has a reputation for going through women like a hot knife through butter. He’s a bad boy with a bad reputation. There’s a darkness within and he has an incredibly short fuse – he’s suffered so badly in his past. The people who should have been there for him and loved him have turned their back on him when he needed them most. Now, he has a small entourage of people close to him, those that he trusts and he is fiercely protective of them and is incredibly slow to trust.<br><br>I don’t think it’s even possible to find the words to express just now much I loved Remy but I will try. He’s an absolute tower of physical strength but inside he’s deeply flawed and is incredibly vulnerable and so unbelievably complex. Experience has taught him to observe, to hold back and to say very little but that steely blue gaze is incredibly expressive and conveys more than he could ever put into words. Despite his obvious powerful physical strength, there’s a vulnerability in there that is so mesmerising and brings out all my protective instincts – I wanted to run my hand down his face, rub my thumb across his bottom lip and tell him that it’s all going to be OK. He wants Brooke with a passion but knows he needs to hold back – he’s so incredibly intense that it’s going to be all or nothing and he needs her to learn about his ‘darkness’ before he can let herself go and allow him to take her.<br><br><b>

</b><br><br>As a man of very few words, he uses songs to tell Brooke how he is feeling by playing her songs on her iPod so she can listen to the lyrics. I loved how Katy Evans did this, how carefully she chose her songs and, as the book progressed, the songs they chose for each other made my eyes shimmer with unshed tears. I was losing it and fast. This is the song that Remy chooses for Brooke - Iris by The Goo Goo Dolls.<br><br><i>
  And I’d give up forever to touch you …<br>Cause I know that you feel me somehow…<br>You’re the closest to heaven that I’ve ever been and I don’t want to go home right now…
